In this manner, O sons, since I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, by its completion it will be understood, and by its expositions, and by its declarations, it is to me apparent that I should commit it to you as a treatise on surgery.
Since the art of surgery is in our region and in our time greatly neglected, thus bringing great peril to the science of it and the instruments of it are lost; only a few small descriptions remain in the books of the ancients, which have become obsolete and led to errors and superstition until its intentions and meanings are veiled and its power and art elongated.
It is apparent to me that I shall revive the order of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and because it will come with the forms of the cautery instruments and the other tools of the work along with the addition of the explanation, and preparation of them, which is necessary.
But the reason why no good craftsman is found with his art in this our time, is because the art of medicine is long and that its practitioner must first be exercised in the science of anatomy, which includes knowledge of the members and their forms, as well as their connection and separation; and have understanding of bones, nerves and ligaments, and their numbers, and their growth; and of pulsating veins and quiet ones, and the sites of their emergence.
And for this reason it is said by Hippocrates that a name is nothing, but in the work small and particularly in the art of the hand.
But we have already said of this in the introduction of this book; since whoever is not knowledgeable about anatomy will not be excused if he falls into error, and thus men will die from it, as I have seen many times, because others are misinformed about this science and deny it and its experiments.
Since I saw a foolish and experienced doctor incise an abscess of the neck on a woman's collarbone, and cut some arteries in the neck so that much blood flowed out before the woman died among her family.
And I saw another doctor who believed that he could extract a stone from a man who was in pain, and the stone was large, and it came to him and extracted the stone with a piece of the bladder, causing the man to die on the third day.
And I called for it to be pulled out, and I saw that due to the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, it was clear that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who took payment from a duke of our land for surgery, and went to a blacksmith who was in debt to him due to a fracture in his hip; and the ignorant doctor prepared him by extracting the fracture through the wound with tendons and spikes with strong construction, but did not leave space for breathing.
And loosen according to his wishes, and lay him flat, and allow him to lie still for several days and command that we release him from the bindings; and remain in this state until the thigh and leg are abscessed, and it leads to ruin.
And I was called to him, prepared to release the bindings, and achieved tranquility and allowed him to endure his pains.
But corruption had already been confirmed in the member, so it could not be stopped, and the corruption spread throughout the limb until the patient died.
And I saw another doctor who lanced an abscess of cancer and it became ulcerated near the owner in several days, causing the evil of it to increase greatly.
The cause is that the cancerous cautery is clean of melancholic humor, so it should not be applied to any part, but rather to a member that is hostile to it.
Therefore, sons, the art of surgery must be divided into two categories: one is associated with health, and the other with danger in greater preparations.

And therefore I will explain that cauterizing, in general terms, applies to all materials or its materials, with the exception of two cases, which are cases without material.
In the dry and hard material case, there is disagreement; some say that cauterizing is beneficial in this case, but others say the opposite, that cauterizing is not appropriate for a disease that is due to quality and dryness, because the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and it is inappropriate for a dry and hard disease to be treated with something that is hot and dry.
And he who says otherwise argues that cauterizing is beneficial for all dry and hard diseases in the human body, because when you compare the human body and its humidity to the nature of fire, the body of a man burns.
And I will explain through experience that I have tried in some cases.

And know, my sons, that the secret of healing by cauterizing with fire and the goodness of it is due to cauterization with burning medicine, because fire is simple, whose action does not extend beyond the member being cauterized, but affects only the adjacent members minimally with a small harm.
However, the action of burning medicine extends to adjacent members and strong heat brings disease in difficult-to-heal and weak places.

And I say that cauterizing is appropriate in all times, because the harmful effects of time are submerged in the benefit of cauterizing, and even more so if cauterizing is for pain or necessary pain, strong fistulas, which cannot tolerate delay because there is fear of worsening, which is greater than a small harm caused by the passage of time.

A more common saying is that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, and it is said to be righteous, but I do not think that this is a cure that benefits from medicine or any other reason to use caution.
The reasoning behind saying that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is not that it is administered as a means of treatment in certain diseases, but rather when those treatments do not work, and at the end of the disease, caution is applied and it does benefit. Then hereafter let it be known that caution is the last remedy of medicine, not according to the reasoning that I understand from the common sayings and tropes of foolish doctors.
The ancients said that gold cautery is better than iron cautery, and they did not say this only because of the equality of gold and the nobility of its substance.
The ancients said that the place for cautery does not burn, although this is not absolutely true, because I have already proven and verified that it does not do so in some bodies, and cautery with gold is better than with iron as they said; however, when you use fire with gold cautery, it is not declared to you, because it depends on the amount you want according to the gold's rugor (malleability), and it must be prepared to be cooled; and if you adjust it over the fire and some layers are created in the fire due to the artificer's occupation with that.
And for this reason, cautery must be made with iron more gently and gradually to correct the operation.

Secondly:
Of the head's cautery.
If chronic and long-lasting pain occurs in the entire head of a patient and it persists despite using tools such as lances, hooks, capsules, plasters, guaze, cudgels, and bandages, among others, and if it has already been cauterized with one cautery without any improvement for that cause, then consider whether the patient's head is of a strong constitution in nature; and if it is not frail and weak, use another cautery to a small extent. Cauterize that area on the corner of his head with a cautery that separates the skin. Cut the skin and expose the amount that has been cauterized, then cauterize that area again in the lower back of the head at the location known as the "basin" (and this is the location where a blister forms). And leave your hand in that place, and do not expose the bone because the patient experiences a great deal of pain different from the pain caused by other head cauterizations.
Label this cautery in its place, because it is more subtle than the cautery used to cauterize the corners and occiput of the head, and this is how it should be done.
Seventhly:
On modern migration treatments.
When a sudden pain in the head occurs, or pain inside the skull spreads, it should be treated with medications that alleviate pain, and other treatment, which I have mentioned in the guidelines for diseases; and if all this does not help, cauterization is performed in two ways: either cauterization with a hot burning medicine, or with iron.
Heat up the alum in a pot, excavate it and expose both ends of the pot. Then make an incision in the location of the pain on the temple with a sharp lance that is deep enough to expose the bone but not visible from outside.
Then apply pressure on the wound using bandages for constant compression, and leave it for three hours; then remove the alum, let the wound heal for two or three days, and apply a dressing soaked in oil until the area becomes dry.
And take care of it until it heals.
And if you wish, do this with some burning medications which I have written about in the second treatise on burning medications.

Chapter V.
On the cauterization of ear pain.
When pain occurs in the ear due to cold and is treated with cooling agents and other cures as mentioned in the division, but the pain persists, then ignite the cautery, called puntum, which has the following form:

And if you make points with the cautery around the entire ear, and that does not help, then cure the spots until they heal.
Chapter VI.
On the cauterization of burns.
A burn that has been treated and then cauterized is not a burn of the kinds that come from poison, as we have said in the divisions of diseases.
Avoid cauterizing the type of burn caused by dryness or spasm of the nerve.
When you treat that type of burn with herbs and poultices, and your cure is not effective, then it is necessary for you to cauterize the patient with three cauteries: the first should be the razit of the aurelha, the second a small one at its temple, and the third the junction of two lips.
Pause your cautery on the side of the diseased area, because softening is not seen in the diseased area but only in the healthy area.
The method of cauterization is to cauterize the area with a cautery at the end of the ear above a small amount on the tip of the head, and at the temple another, the length of which should be equal to the length of the finger, and pause your hand with the cautery until the burned area has been covered by the thickness of the skin layer.
And this is the form of the cautery, which is the shape of a knife, the shape of which is flat. But it is necessary that this one be very thin, as you will see; and it is necessary to sharpen the knife in excessively rough places a little.
And cure the area with what is before processing until it heals.

Chapter X.
On the cauterization of epilepsy.
Epilepsy is not cauterized unless it is due to a fever.
And so it is necessary to treat the brain of the patient at the beginning with warm and cold treatments, as well as other care that has been mentioned in the previous division when the patient is severe and tolerates the exception of medications.
If the patient is a child who does not tolerate medications, administer gargles and mouthwashes that are meant to soothe the stomach, for several days, with good nutrition.
Then shave the patient's head, and cauterize it at the proper location on the head according to the method previously described, and another cauterization on the back of the neck, and one on each corner of the head. And if the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize that area with a heated iron, having paralysis and softening of the body over the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back.
Then heat the iron as previously described.
But if the patient is a child, then pause the subtle cautery in this manner.

The patient should be seated and held from all sides.

Make the patient do this every week once, with other good treatment until he is well; or if you wish, cauterize it by making small points as much as possible, without having a hand always with such an arranged iron: this is a type of cautery that keeps the brain moist.
Then apply it to the affected area in a remedy or liniment made from quinine.

Chapter XVI.
On cauterizing the eyelid of an eye when the hair turns into parts inside and the eye swells.
When the hair of an eye turns into parts inside and swells, cauterize them in two ways: either by burning or with a medicine-burning method.
If by burning cauterization, command the patient to wash their hair as they would when grooming; continue this until the hair grows back and disappears. If it inflames, then you must burn the eyelashes, placing a bandage over them so that no moisture enters until the hair grows out again.
Therefore, when the hair grows back and disappears, place a bandage on the patient's head near the eyelid of their eye and apply a sign with tweezers according to the shape of a holly leaf, starting from where the eyelashes are growing.
And place cotton soaked in alum or egg white on the eye.
Place fire under the cautery, which has this shape:
Place the cautery on the shape you marked, little by little, in observed patches, until the surface of the cystic area, which is similar to holly leaves, is completely burned.
The sign of healing in this work is that you observe the eyelid of an eye becoming contracted and the eyelashes lifted due to the puncture of the eye.
Therefore, lift it with your hand for three days and place a cotton dressing over it until the scar rises up. Cure that one with warm liquid until it is healed.
However, if the eyelashes return for some reason and the eyelid becomes soft again, then do another cauterization on it as you did initially.
However, if the eyelashes are in the eyelid, cauterize it until it returns to its original position, heals, and the eyelashes do not irritate the eye.
The cautery method using medicine burns is when you command the patient to wash their hair until it grows back and disappears; then make a paper with cloth in the shape of a holly leaf.
And take known sage and live coal and place them on top. (It seems there is a mistake or incomplete line here, as no text appears to follow this symbol.) And place the medicine on the affected area and gently press it, but do not let the patient feel the burning sensation of the medicine; for a sensation like fire is painful.
Therefore, when you perceive that the burn sensation has stopped, remove the medicine and apply a cool substance to it; then wash the eye with water; and consider whether the eyelid is raised as it should be after washing with heat or incision, for in this case there will be no more inflammation. If the eyelash returns to its previous state due to the medicine, place the medicine back on the affected area where there was no pressure applied, and do not let it degrade until your procedure is complete and the eye has healed.
And place pressure on the area to be cauterized until the abscess is eradicated, and care for it with gauze or something else until it heals.

which is convex, like the shape of a reed or quill, with one end where the cautery is applied.

Chapter XIX.
On cauterizing a fistula in the mouth.
When an abscess forms on the uvula or palate or between the teeth and becomes pus, make an incision and it bursts, and if it is old, break it open, and burn the abscess and make a fistula, and treat it as I have previously mentioned. If treatment is not effective, you must cauterize with the amount received in the fistula, hold the heated iron in the fistula opening, and repeat this process once or twice; then treat it with the ointment I have mentioned until healed.
And if the abscess is drained and heals, that is good; but if not, it is necessary to expose the location and burn the rotten bone according to its respective chapter.
Chapter XX.
On cauterizing teeth and softening gums.
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth are bad, but treatment with medicines is ineffective, place the patient's head on your lap, hold the cautery rod in the shape described below (see illustration), place the handle of the cautery rod on the tooth and insert the heated cautery into the gum quickly so that you hold it there until the heat from the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
Lift your hand, and repeat the cauterizing process as desired.
Then have the patient rinse his mouth with salt water and hold it for an hour, then spit it out, as the bad tooth is closed and the softened gum is strengthened, and the moisture is dried up.
Chapter XXI.
On cauterizing tooth pain.
When tooth pain is due to coldness, or it is inflamed or worm-ridden, and treatment with medicine is not effective, you can cauterize it using two methods: either cauterizing with a cattle brand or cauterizing with fire.
Cautery with a pointed tip should be taken, which is made of cow's horn and iron handle, then take care to wrap it in linen and cover the tip of the cautery, immerse it in hot water, and place it on the painful tooth hastily until it becomes numb.
Then repeat this process several times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, immerse linen or cloth in the aforementioned cautery and place it on the painful tooth, then place the heated iron on top of it until the iron reaches the root of the cavity of the tooth.
However, cauterization with fire may be harmful if there is an ulcer or abscess in the area and the heat of the fire does not reach the patient's mouth.
Then hold the heated cautery in the form you choose, place it on the tooth and keep your hand on it until the cauterization is numb; do this several times as needed for the pain to subside or on that day or the next.
And note that for the aforementioned cauterization, the patient must keep their mouth open with good force and hold the cautery for an hour, then spit it out; this is the method of using the cautery.
And cauterize as much affected area as you are able to reach.

Chapter XXII.
On the cauterization of hernias.
When hernias are of the phlegmatic type and are not obedient to medications for digestion, if you want to promote digestion of that type, then heat the cautery with this shape (as follows): having two handles extended so that smoke comes out from the other end, hold the cautery by the handle and heat it with fire, then place it on the abscess once, and if necessary, repeat until the abscess is cauterized to the root.
If the abscess is small, then place the cautery on it according to its size, and leave it for three days and place it on top of linen soaked in oil until what the fire has burned away is gone.
And care for it with rinsing, dressings, and bandages until it is healed.

On the cauterization of throat ulcers and constriction of veins.

Cauterize that with another cautery at the joint of the neck in the lower vertebrae of it. The cautery should be round like a nail, following the previous method (i.e., as described earlier).
Care for it with what has been prescribed earlier until it is healed.

Capital XXVI [Chapter 26]
On cauterization of the stomach.
When humidity and motes occur in the stomach and multiply its roominess, and if you continue with the methods of treatment without conferring [something], it is necessary that the patient be laid on their back, extend their limbs and chest, and then cauterize it with three cauterizations: one cautery placed under the feet for the thickness of a finger, a pointed cautery, and two cauteries placed under the ribs of the cautery until the triangular figure of the cauterization appears; elongate those that are not adjusted to avoid pus formation.

Capital XXVII [Chapter 27]
On cauterization of the inflamed liver.
When pain occurs in the liver due to coldness, humidity, or windiness to such an extent that it is expelled from its normal position by superfluous egression, and the patient is cured with what has been said without conferring [something], it is necessary that the patient be laid on their back, and sign three cauterizations according to this form and this quantity on the liver under the hypochondriac region, so that the patient's head lies downwards.

And it is possible for you to cauterize these cauteries with a cautery knife, when you have the skill and discretion in this art.
Be careful not to overdo the cauterization, let the medicine be applied to the entire body so that it reaches the intestines, as the body here is delicate, and know this.
Chapter 28.
On the incision of an abscess in the thigh with cauterization.
When you are about to excise or drain an abscess in the thigh and want to know if the abscess is located in the muscle of the thigh or in its sheath (fascia), then, if it is in the muscle of the thigh, the patient feels a heaviness and the pain does not worsen.
If it is in the sheath (fascia) of the thigh, then the pain becomes more intense and often exhausts the doctors in its treatment.
Therefore, the patient should lie facing downwards; and approach the abscess site with caution; and heat the cauterization tool, which resembles a rope, as described in the previous page. Cauterize with the hot cautery tool until all the affected area is burned, until it reaches the abscess (sinus), until pus comes out.
Take care of the rest of the abscesses until they are healed.
And it is not necessary to use this cauterization method alone, but rather the one studied in the art of medicine, which has been practiced for many illnesses; however, some experienced practitioners may perform this operation differently, but you should follow the prescribed procedure and it will be better.
Chapter 29.
On the cauterization of ulcers (lesions).
The ancient cauterizations of arthritic ulcers are performed by treating them as plagues, according to this method; and you should take a long, dry arrow (lance) from the arthritic razor collection, and it should be thick like a finger.
Then immerse the arrow (lance) in oil and heat it over the fire; then cauterize with a small cautery at the location between the base of the neck and the collar, using two smaller cauteries on either side, one slightly lower than the beard, and two on the area that descends between the fifth rib and the nipple, slightly lower at the back; and another on the middle of the thigh, and another on the stomach, and three cauterizations at the back; and another in the location between the shoulders, and two on both sides of the thigh, after the cautery that is between the shoulders.
And it is important not to press too hard with the cauterization tool, but rather let the burn mark be visible on the body.
And it was said by some ancient men that they used a cauterization iron resembling a rod and heated it, placing it in the location between the ribs until it reached the abscess (sinus) and drained pus, as was discussed in the thigh abscess treatment.
But in this incision with cauterization, there is no cause for fear, as death may occur in the location of the fistula that has not healed.
Chapter thirty.
On the cauterization of the spleen.
When treating the illness of the spleen as I have said about its treatment and not confining it to division, you must perform cauterization in three ways, all of which are permissible, one of which is that you make three or four stitches according to the length of the spleen, according to the figure of the cauterizations of the liver, whose figure has been preceded.
And the thickness of each cauterization should be as thick as a finger or slightly more, and the method of cauterization should be the same as the one I have mentioned for liver cauterization.
And do not press your hand against the cauterization, and let the patient lie on their back.
Another method of cauterization is to ignite the cautery with two prongs, which we have mentioned in the chapter on muscle dislocation and raise the patient's left shoulder so that the left side of the spleen lies flat against it.
And raise the shoulder to the height that raises the spine in proportion to the length of the body, so that the cauterizations can be made according to the width of the body.
And bring the two prongs together and ignite them in the area where they penetrate the spleen of the other side.
And withdraw the cautery, so four cauterizations are made.
And if you wish, cauterize with a cautery having three prongs.
And apply the cautery until it has bled for several days, since this is more beneficial than other causes of treatment mentioned earlier.
Chapter thirty-one.
On the cauterization of dropsy.
Do not cauterize in dropsy, but rather incise it specifically.
When treating dropsy with the methods of treatment I have mentioned and not confining it to division, you must therefore cauterize with four cauterizations around the navel, one on the stomach, another on the liver, another on the spleen, two between the vertebrae of the back, one at the right hip, and another on the stomach. And the depth of the cauterization should be proportional to the thickness of the skin.
And let the cautery remain open for a long time so that it bleeds profusely.
And do not evacuate the patient from treatment near the cauterization with anything that requires them to be moved away from it, as this will hasten their recovery with assistance.
The shape of the cautery used to cauterize the abdomen should be club-shaped, as described earlier, and that used for the back should be olive-shaped, as described earlier in its shape.
Chapter thirty-two.
On the cauterization of feet and other things.
When the feet are swollen in dropsy and filled with stagnant water, you must cauterize the feet on the back of the foot between the ankle and heel, raise your hand above the cauterization and do not twist it; and lift your hand, but do not completely return it, since stagnant water will run out.
The cautery should be shaped as follows: Make two cauterizations on the two sides of the body, and in each side make a cauterization with the tip of the cautery. And the cautery should be as long as the body part: one end on top and the other a little lower; and above each body part, two cauterizations.
And let the wound remain open for a long time to allow some water to run out of it.
And treat these causes as I have said earlier.

44th Chapter.
On the cauterization of gout and joint pain.
When joint pain is caused by cold humors that infiltrate each part of the body, and pain occurs in the feet, it is customarily called gout by doctors.

If you wish, take the rod and wrap it in the proper part of it, and apply oil in the concavity of the sore, or juice from some herb, or any medicine of your choice into the catheter - it is in the ear - and press the rod with the proper part and squeeze with your hand to compress it temporarily inside until the oil is expelled in the concavity of the sore and the patient feels the oil inside.
And whatever is stuffed into the ear should be heated slightly with fire. Be careful that the substance you will distill in the ear is not too hot, for medicines of the ear cannot withstand water.
Capital VII.
On the cure of ear blockages.
Sometimes children are born without perforated ventricles from their mothers, and this condition occurs in some men, blockage in the tissue of the ear due to inflammation or non-healing flesh; and this blockage sometimes occurs at the entrance of the ear canal which does not drain, and sometimes it occurs in the outer parts.
That which happens at the front of it (the body part), which is not understood by the patient, is in the greatest dispositions for difficult healing.
In that which you understand by the patient's explanation, it is necessary that you cover the patient's ear to the ground and look at it (the affected area). And if there is an obvious distention, open that with a thin spatula, which is its form.
If the extremity of it (the body part) is small in width, and one side is sharp while the other is not; and the spatula should be of two lion's lengths long to avoid injuring the ear.
And if the obstruction is due to flesh growing in the ear or the meat of it (the body part), you should remove it with a sharp and pointed tool, and cut it off quickly before all the flesh has been removed.
And if the obstruction is in the front of the ear, you should take a thin wire that has been heated slightly with fire and place it in the flesh of the ear.
And if the patient feels obvious obstruction with difficulty breathing, you should try to relieve the obstruction gently without causing harm to the nerves of the ear.
Then cover the ear with cloth of the appropriate size, wrapping it with the Egyptian ointment that you have applied; and do this for several days until you are sure of the healing of the wound or take some other medication and immerse it in water, then crush it into powder and use it according to the instructions; and if the ear is already suppurating, you must remove the pus and replace it with another medicine that you have wrapped in a cotton soaked in rose oil until the suppuration subsides; and care for it until it is healed.
If there is bleeding from the ear, immerse a sponge or cloth in hot water and place it on the ear, and use another treatment to stop the bleeding, which is called "distillation" in the medical treatise.
Kapitel VIII. (Kapitel means chapter)
Vom Behandeln von Augenathese, die sich zu den Augen erstrecken. (Endeveno means to extend towards)
Augenathese, die sich zu den Augen erstrecken und manchmal feucht sind, sind bei einigen Personen trocken. (Endeveno means to extend towards)
Deshalb muss man die Augenathese mit der Hand oder mit einem Instrument, das zum Zerteilen geeignet ist, entfernen und auf den verletzten Stellen eine Pulvermischung anwenden.
Wenn es Schmerzen mit Blutfluss gibt, sollten Sie diese mit einer kleinen glühenden Nadel behandeln.
Die beste Behandlung ist die Entfernung der Schwellungen und trockenen Verletzungen, wenn es noch eine Ursache für die Entstehung ist; und wenn sie mit dem Feuer behandelt werden, verbrennen diese Verletzungen und kehren nicht zurück.
Kapitel IX. (Kapitel means chapter)
Behandlung von großen Augenkrankheiten, die sich zu den Augen erstrecken.
Beim Auftreten von Tumoren in den Augen gibt es eine Ursache, die ähnlich einer großen Krankheit ist und wegen ihrer Größe und Härte auch als solche bezeichnet wird.
Es handelt sich um eine Ansammlung von großer Feuchtigkeit in der Augenlidunter- und -oberseite.
Deshalb untersucht man, ob die Größe der Tumoren durch etwas hervorgerufen wird, das aus dem Auge kommt und überall verbreitet ist; und die Ursache dieses Vorgangs ist unauffällig.
Es sei denn, fürechte die Tumoren durch eine Aussparung in der Länge und entfernt sie mit Mitteln zur Entfernung oder Abschneiden.
If the wound is large, then adjust it with stitches, and take care of it until it heals.
If it is small, you will not suffer harm by allowing the anguent (?) to restore and heal it.
If the swelling is spreading towards the inner parts of the eyelid, you should remove the surface of the eyelid and suspend the swelling with a hook, one that you require for incision, and press it all around, and if the eyelid is elongated by incision, you will not notice anything in any case.
Clean the wound with salt water, and treat the area with something that heals it until it is healed.
Chapter X.
On the treatment of inflammation in the eyelid above the wound.
Inflammation of the eyelid above the wound is grayish in color and is most often found in children, aggravating their wounds and causing their catarrhs to worsen; and they cannot look at the sun due to the tearing of tears at it.
And they often lie on their faces all the time and sleep on their faces; and when their eyelids are wet from below the eyebrows, which have already been covered by inflammation, it appears imminent that infection will occur in the eye; and when you press the area with your fingers, you will feel the infection inside.
One method of operation is when the patient lowers their head into your lap, and you place a cloth over them and apply warm water to it in a circle corresponding to the size of the inflammation, and place that over the inflammation and press with your fingers all around to aggravate infection in the middle of the circle. Then make an opening in the middle of the inflammation with a lancet, making sure that the incision is not larger than the incision made during lancing (lymphotomy).
But in the preparation (of the treatment), it is necessary that you cut open the scrotum entirely until you reach the infection, since in the most favorable cases, the infection may be treated by incision in the form of white pus-like substance.
Then extract it with cloths that you have wrapped between your fingers and turn it with your right and left hands until it is discharged.
And be careful not to adjust the incision so that with the pus you do not reach the eye and damage it.
But if the pus does not appear at the beginning of the incision, you should adjust the incision slightly to facilitate the release of the pus; and then extract it as described earlier; and immerse cloths in warm water and wring them out and place them on the area and press them with sand or something similar.
And let those who have salt and powder it in the hollow of the incision to absorb that remaining moisture.
And take care of it until it is healed.
But if an abscess occurs in the cauterized spot, you should take care of it with ointments made from castor oil until it is healed.
Chapter XI.

Title XII.
On removing hairs that pierce the eye with an awl when the hair is hard.
When the hairs are not natural, hard, rough and piercing the eyes, you should perform the operation by taking a sharp awl, placing it on a soft and supple needle, and ensuring that the ends of the tool are adjusted carefully without any subtle movement. The length of the hairs should be as long as one hand span.
You should make another thin needle near it in short order, and cut the ends of that one if you want to do so.
Place the patient's head in your lap and position it facing you so that your work is visible, since this operation is delicate and requires precision.
Approach the needle into the incision of the skin carefully adjusted that requires suturing, and make it penetrate quickly into the eyelid before drawing it out through the skin naturally.
Then pull the hair up and insert the thread into it (or them), and ensure that there are one or two or three but not more.
Then tie your hand around it where the hair has been pulled out, inserting the thread into the eyelid and pulling it through naturally.
If the stitching is not done and the hair has not been pulled out, you should insert the thread at the sides of the wound that you have made and tied with the same thread, until it emerges through the skin above the wound.
And wait for the wound to heal, because when you have inserted and tied the stitching, you should press on the swelling and clamp it with forceps, leaving them in place for two or three days until the hair adheres to its location and grows over it well.
If the hair is too short, then you should take a longer natural hair and tie it to the one that has been pulled out, lifting it up or letting it grow until it reaches an appropriate space, and continue lifting it upwards.
Chapter XIII.
On the treatment of echydris that occurs in the upper eyelid.
When an echydris (sty) appears in the eyelid and is caused by contraction of the eyelid when it is pulled to one side due to poor healing from a wound or burn, it is called leprosy, and this type of echydris can be either natural or accidental, caused by poor healing from a wound or burn, or resembling them in appearance.
The method of operation is to make an incision in the consolidation and separate the lips of it, and place a piece of linen cloth between them, and tie them together until they are healed.
It is necessary to treat the cause of the echydris that causes it to recur, since if you do not do so, the echydris will return even worse than before.
Use remedies that soften the cause, such as fenugreek, and wrap it in water in which it has been boiled with its seeds, or gum tragacanth, which should be liquefied with one of the oils, and immerse the cloth in it and treat with it.
The secret to your treatment is to perform all procedures without causing any further consolidation according to the original form.
This operation that we have described is not only a correction of echydris but also serves to restore the original shape of the affected area.
Chapter XIV.
On the treatment of echydris that occurs in the lower eyelid.
The echydris that occurs in the lower eyelid is called true echydris; it can be either natural or accidental.
Accidental echydris is caused by a wound, burn, or other similar factors.
The method of operation for this is to take a needle with double thread and insert it into the skin, making it pass from the tear duct on the left side to the tear duct on the right side until the thread reaches both ends of the skin.
Then stretch the skin to the sides with the needle and sew it up with the needle, making an incision with a large scalpel. And if the eye shape returns as it should be, that is good; otherwise, take the ray and place it in the split figure, then turn the eyelid and make two openings on the sides of the eyelid from its hinge.
The extremities of the two fissures should be made at two angles of the incision, which you have already made up to where they converge, and the angle should be made such that when they come together, a figure is formed from them.
And this figure is the Greek letter lambda.
Then remove the flesh to the extent of the acute angle's width, ensuring that it is sufficient for the eyelid.
Then adjust the separated parts and sew them with cotton thread, and take care of them with the medicine for softening and blisters until they are healed.
And if you are incising through a fissure or suture or cauterization, then you must open it with a flat incision on the skin of the eyelid as previously described. Then separate the blister between the two lips as previously mentioned.
In the summary of the sermon on the treatment of incision, whether above or below, it runs in operation according to its preparation, and that shape is in the form of various motes.
And the skilled craftsman always prepares an instrument in every way that is possible for him to return the figure to its natural shape or as close as possible, and the patient according to what is necessary for the operation and tools in the best arrangement.
Chapter XV.
On the adhesion of the eyelid with the conjunctiva or the cornea.
When this consolidation occurs in many men who have the eyelid adhered to the cornea or conjunctiva, and it is solidified above the lid and the albumen of the white, prohibiting the ease of movement and its natural functions, therefore you must go under the edge of the ray from below the eyelid and lift it upwards, or stretch it with oil.
Then you must incise the adhesion with a thin spatula that is not as sharp as an incision, having a blunt tip so that the patient is not disturbed by the operation, and remove the spatula without damaging the white with its point.
And your incision should be such that it separates the adhesion with ease until the eyelid returns to its natural shape and the entire adhesion is healed.
Then put salt water on the white, with which you wash it; or distill in its place a solution of rosewater diluted in water.
Then separate the eyelid and conjunctiva with blistering fluid, and place cotton wool soaked in albumen of egg white on the conjunctiva, and apply the third day causes for consolidation until it is healed.

Chapter .19.
On the reduction of an arrowhead into the nose.

Chapter .20.
Reduction of the hernia swelling
When the hernia swells completely and there is no harmful consequence or reduction, then you must first make the patient lie down, place them on their back with pillows under their head, and place cold compresses on the neck without cutting it; and then apply a liniment over the hernia that has been made from castor oil, aloe, honey, and sarcocolla, and firmly press the plaster onto the hernia with lots of powder.
The method of powders is to take cloth made from lion's wool, and each piece should be folded into four layers; make powder from those pieces.
Then apply the powder one on top of the other according to the quantity needed for the hernia. Then press hard with a thick, strong cloth and tight binding, and repeat the compresses without cutting; remove the dressings, loosen the hernia and allow it to rest during the day and night.
But if in the meantime, the ligament becomes softened, then it must be made tighter.
And remove the dressing during the day and night as I said earlier.
And if the hernia has already been reduced, then that is good; otherwise, apply the plaster with powders and tight binding and compresses until it is healed.
Chapter 21.
On the incision of the protruding uveal tunica (eye sac).

Chapter 22.
On the treatment of ulcers.
This ulcer which is called an ulcer is not simply watery discharge from the wound, but it is something else.
The method of working on it is to make the patient sit over a prepared and straight seat, and then take hold of his head with both hands and push him down so that you can see the discharge coming out from the wound, and let it dry and do not let it descend, and keep the light on, and let the patient see the cause in this way as he used to.
And if it does not go down (the discharge), then you know that it is water.
However, if the discharge is not prepared with what we have said, then make the patient sit between your hands and take a thin spatula and press it on the conjunctiva at the junction of the cornea in the cornea (at the appropriate location), until the discharge is removed.
Therefore, when the discharge is removed, you distill water from the wound in which you have mixed honey or water in which you have boiled fennel and honey.
And let it be treated with other causes until it heals.
Chapter 22.
On the treatment of the water flowing from the wound.
We have already said the species of water in the division and which should be pierced with the medicine declaring it, then that one according to its health.
Then you must make the patient sit between your hands on a chair and hold his wound tight.

Then press the eyelid and feel that almadra has been brought out due to your action.

And let it rest for a little while; so if the water has come out, then you pause another moment before letting go of almadra.

But those of us from our time bind the swollen area with warm water.

Chapter XXIV.
On the treatment of skin growths in the nose.
When in the nose are born diverse skins associated with some cause that resembles the scorpion movement of legs, or polyps feet; and this disease is called polyps because it resembles that foot represented. It is cancerous flesh, ulcerated, of dark color; and it is not a lion's flesh that is dark in color.

Eradication of Teeth.
It is necessary that you cure the tooth of its pain with every means and take great care in the entire eradication of it, because there is no need for further observation when it is eradicated, because it is a superfluous substance during the eradication of it.
However, when the patient is ready to have that tooth removed, you must certainly be certain which tooth is causing the pain, because many times the pain deceives the patient and makes them believe that a healthy tooth is causing it, and you remove that one and the pain does not cease until the diseased and painful tooth has been removed, as we have seen in barber surgeries.
Therefore since you must be certain which tooth is causing the pain and know this well, you should then make an incision around the tooth with spittle containing some virtue, until it has dissolved the tooth from the gums on all sides, and then apply a hot iron (perhaps a branding iron) or thin forceps gently to loosen it bit by bit until it is extracted.
Then apply alcohol (possibly a strong spirit) with forceps to hold it firmly and place the patient's head between your hands so that you can hold it securely, and extract the tooth carefully in a straight motion without breaking it or causing further pain to the patient.
And therefore if this is not forgotten, you should then take one of those instruments and place it under the tooth with ease and exert force to remove it in the same way as was described at the beginning.
However, if the tooth is fractured or decayed, you must then wrap it in cloth and tighten it with a thin wire at the root to prevent it from being broken during your constriction on it with forceps.
And you must work carefully around the incision in the gums and be aware of your strength so as not to break it and leave a piece behind, and return to the patient for any pain that is greater than the initial pain from the procedure.
And beware that you do not do what some ignorant barbers do in their reckless and hasty dental extractions, since they do not administer what we have recommended; for many times this results in large infections that are difficult to treat, and all the roots remain, or some of them remain, or you extract it with some bones from the jaw as has been testified by many.
And for the removal of it (the affected area), wash the mouth with vinegar or salt water.
If there are flows of blood from this place, proceed as with a wound cauterized, then take some vinegar and sprinkle it on the affected area, if that does not stop the bleeding, cauterize it.
The form of the forceps and tweezers with which you begin to extract the tooth should be long, short and thick so that they are not bent when you have to use them.
And as with large hands that go deep within but are not bent, they should be short.
They should be made of Indian steel and properly made straight shafts, and in the shafts there should be teeth that interlock with each other and tighten by forcefully constricting, and sometimes the shafts should have the shape of an heron's beak (ciconia), which is called a claw, and they should be strong.

Chapter 40.
In which is the summary of the speech on the opening of ulcers and their section.
Ulcers are special kinds of wounds in various ways, as memory of them recalls, of each one in this book.
They are diverse in the method of their opening and section by two ways, one of which is by the nature of ulcers themselves; and because they obstruct fluids.
The second method is specifically for the places where accidents of the body occur, because an ulcer that occurs in the head is different from an ulcer that occurs in the buttocks; and an ulcer in a fleshy place is different from an ulcer in a joint; and each of them has its own treatment by operation.
Moreover, some ulcers require that they not be opened except when the wound is matured or completed in them.
Other ulcers that require opening when they are ripe and not before their completion, such as ulcers near joints, because an ulcer near a joint takes longer to heal until the pus that surrounds it is purged, and it weakens or corrupts the ligaments or nerves of that joint, causing contraction of that member; or an ulcer on a main part, if you delay opening it until it is matured, it can harm the main part; or one in the buttocks, which should not be opened before it matures; and it is not necessary to open a wound that is not ripe except for a wound in the buttocks, because you cannot insert your finger into it and it can elongate towards the parts inside the buttocks, and a fistula is formed or one is made at the edge of it that does not heal. Moreover, you must know when to open the ulcer, and this is when it is ripe.
And you should know that it is ripe when the pain subsides and fever stops, and the decrease in swelling and pulse, and the sharpening of the ulcer head, and other signs.
And because you must know that opening should be done in the place most distant from the ulcer and where pus is coming from healing of the edge.
Opening is sometimes done along the flesh or the body if ulcers are in the groin or feet, and areas of ligaments, tendons, nerves, arteries; and in particular, in all places that do not reflect; because in those that reflect, use opening according to the member.
When the ulcer is in a fleshy place, it is better to allow confirmation of the digestion of it according to its completion, as we have said; because if you open it beforehand, the wound deepens and becomes more inflamed, and the edges of it are hardened and the depth increased.
Some ulcers are opened according to the thickness of the flesh or body as necessary, or according to what the member needs.
And it is necessary to administer a small opening, and in large ulcers a large and wide or deep cuts according to the diversity of the size of the ulcers.
Other ulcers are those in which it is necessary for the edges to be concave and cut when they are opened in such a way that a pouch or abscess has already formed, like an ulcer that occurs in double areas and boils.
And of those that are incised with a section having three corners; and of those is one that is incised like the figure of a myrtle leaf, like ulcers in joints.
And of them is one that round and crescent-shaped section are administered, and similar to those.
However, one that is not like them, such as superficial ulcers of lions, you should open it with a superficial or flat incision only.
And when the ulcer is large and has collected a lot of pus, you should open it and not try to remove all the pus at that time; after removing part of it, leave the ulcer open for another day, and after removing a larger part, make several observations according to gradation until it is forgotten.
Furthermore, if the patient is a green-eyed man or woman, or a small child, or an old person in decrepitude, because animal spirits are weakened by the release of pus many times, and the patient dies, you should not operate on them.
Take great care with this chapter, and make sure your puncture is accurate where you pierce these abscesses, as you must avoid wounding the surrounding area and consider whether the abscess wound is small or flat, in which case you can use a lancet or an ancient method; but if the abscess is large and the fissures of the puncture are many, you must stop every now and then to allow them all to heal simultaneously.
If part of the abscess is detached from the skin or if you have concaved it in its circumference, you must compress it with an old cloth or thread made from linen, as when bread or razors are sterilized, without moisture; and keep it inside for three days; and apply pressure on it and treat it with what is necessary to prevent infection until it is healed.
If bleeding occurs during your operation, you provide cold water and wine vinegar in which a linen cloth is soaked, and place it over the location of the multiple bleeding spots observed.
If the bleeding continues, you must administer treatment and medication as recommended in various locations of this book and division.
If it is winter and the location of the abscess is near many nerves, you must apply powder in wine and oil of caution, and place it over the affected areas.
If it is summer and the affected areas are fleshy, you must place powders moistened in water or oil or wine and apply them frequently until the third day, as mentioned earlier, and you should then remove the abscess and prevent it from becoming infected while providing it with appropriate treatment until it is healed.
This is what is required for the knowledge of the treatment of abscesses universally, but according to the division I have already mentioned for each type of abscess and the specific methods of their cure in separate chapters.

On incision of abscesses that appear on the skin of the head.
On small abscesses on the skin of the head, and those that contain special types of nodes with tunics made for them; and the various types of their locations.

In the section of all, and in the extraction of those [things], there is no fear, for the extraction of those things does not hinder archery.
The operation in the section of those things is that you use an instrument of the shape which approaches closely to them, called entromes, until you know what it contains.
But if what it contains is moisture, then you should divide it with a section according to its length by means of a shallow incision in the following manner:
And begin at the section of line B up to line G. Then, when the moisture is evacuated, you should excise that part which contains the moisture, and be careful not to leave any cause for it whatsoever, because too much observation returns if there remains some cause.
And immerse the wound in Egyptian clay if it is present, or, if not, in water and salt; fill the wound with that mixture and leave it until another day, because with this you corrode everything that remains of the skin.
And repeat the treatment with Egyptian clay several times if necessary, until you are confident that there remains no cause for the skin; then take care of the wound with Egyptian clay until it is healed.
And if an abscess contains greasy nodes, you should incise it in this manner: The incision should have the shape of a cross, and cut it between two lips of the incision and pull it out from all sides, exerting your strength in the extraction of the sac containing it.
However, if your archery is hindered by this, do what I told you earlier.
And treat an abscess with lancing and care according to what I earlier told you; lancing an abscess is easier because it has less blood and less moisture.
And sometimes these abscesses are in the head of some men who have none of it (humidity); this cause is because I lanced an abscess on an old woman's head like hard, rough, white stone, which could not be pierced, and if anyone struck it, they would be injured.
However, in other abscesses occurring in the head, this is not the subject of this chapter, such as abscesses that occur on the heads of children and which you should lance the auricles, but the incision for these shall be a shallow incision.
And pause the perforation of those from the lower part so that the body will be relieved at the lower incisions.
And take care of them with what is appropriate for their treatment.
Chapter 42.
On the incision of scrofulas which occur in the neck.
Many times these abscesses deeply enter the neck and the armpits and the groin, and sometimes they occur in other parts of the body.
And those that occur in the neck are divided into two: those that originate from within it and all scrofulas of these are distinguished by their own sac, as in the nodes and abscesses of the head, as we earlier recommended.
And the types of these scrofulas are either hard or soft, those that contain moisture being soft, and those that are malignant should not be treated with care.
Therefore, in the one that you see well-positioned in the Touching, of which the color of what is apparent is similar to that of kelp and is bad throughout, and is not attached to the nerve of the neck, nor to the veins, nor to the archery, and is movable, it is necessary that you incise it with a shallow incision from the upper part of the body to the lower part of the body along the line of G to B, and scrape it from all sides, and cut two lips of the kelp with scissors or with a knife if necessary, as we have said in the abscesses of the head, and extract it bit by bit.
And it is more caution not to incise the vein or nerve.
And let the spatula not be too sharp, which may adjust your hand to the incision or upset the patient, and that you incise what is not necessary to incise; because if you incise a vein or artery and forbid yourself from continuing the operation, you should pause in the wound treated with quicklime or other powders that cause bleeding, clean the wound, and leave it until the acidity of the abscess subsides and the wound becomes soft and porous. When the blood is separated (or drained)
Then return to your operation before it was completed.
And find out if there are any other small scrofula (abscesses), so that you may incise them and clean them up.
And if the large vein is involved in the abscess, cover it so that you do not incise the abscess at its base. Bind it well with a strong bandage and let it heal within itself without any harm.
And fill the wound with old lard (or ointment) that you have already applied, and take care of it.
And if you incise the entire abscess, then ensure that you close the two edges of the wound and suture it as soon as possible to prevent any excess leakage.
But if you see that there is an excess leakage due to the large size of the abscess, then understand to incise the base of it, drain it, and provide stitching and treatment for it.
And for abscesses containing moisture (pus), make a superficial perforation where the abscess is about to mature and pause the perforation of the pus that rises from the body's base, as we said earlier.
And apply perforation (or lancing), using lard or similar substances to corrode the infected material. When you see that the wound is clean, care for it with fresh meat-based ointment until it heals.
Chapter XLIII. (43)
On the incision of a gangrenous appendix in the gallbladder (or abscess).
The ancients performed this incision on the appendix, and I have never seen it done in our land.
And this is the inscription of their (ancient) discourse.
But in men with obstruction (of the gallbladder), the removal of the appendix should be avoided, as it does not benefit the patient because all the veins and major vessels are nearby.
But in those who have appendixes infected with abscess or gallbladder or double earlobe (gallstones), when the illness is not in the bladder, it is necessary to perform the incision of the appendix to avoid death caused by strangulation.
Therefore, when we wish to incise the appendix, we should make the incision three circles from the gallbladder's circles or four with a smaller section along the length between two circles according to size, ensuring that the incision is in the cephac (the body of the gallbladder) and not the cartilage. This location is suitable for incision as it lacks muscle and the veins supplying blood are nearby.
And if the surgeon is inexperienced, extend the cord of the gallbladder by an inch and make a split in the cord up to the channel, but avoid veins supplying blood if possible.
And make a split in the cipallus (gallbladder) as recommended; this refers to the incision of the channel through the flap that is at its exit and where there is damage or abscess of the bladder.
Leave the wound open for some time.
So that the fear of perforation is removed, sew together two edges of the cord of the wound and only stitch it without the cartilage.
And apply medicines that make the flesh heal.
Albucasis says that the essence of the recommended discourse is to open the gallbladder of those who have appendixes infected with abscess and the patient has already died, and the intestines are cut, and someone goes to incise the epiglottis so that the patient can breathe through the wound for some respiration, and thus be saved from death.
Therefore, I command that the wound be left open until the malice of the illness is consumed, which takes three days; and once this is done, I command to sew up the wound and care for it until it heals.
And what I have seen personally is that a woman took a knife and put it in her own gallbladder and incised one part of the lung, and I was called to treat her, and I found the wound infected like the breath of the dying, and I exposed the wound and found that blood was leaking from the small wound.
Therefore, I was confessed that she had not incised a vein or ligature, and the wind came from the wound, and I treated it until it healed.
And the woman did not recur in the bladder if there was no improvement in her condition, and another few days were allowed for her recovery.
And now I say that in the incision of the appendix, there is no fear.
Chapter XLIV (44)
On the incision of an abscess that occurs in the gallbladder outside, which is called a hernia of the gallbladder.
The abscess called hernia of the gallbladder is a large abscess according to the color of the body and it occurs in women.
It is according to two methods, whether it is natural or accidental.
In the natural case, it is not necessary to treat.
The accidental case is according to two methods of which the first is similar to fatty nodes, and the second method is similar to an abscess that is made by the constriction of an artery, and in this case there is fear. It is not necessary to make a presumption of the patient unless it is small. You should investigate that and observe it with the said method, and if you find something similar to fatty nodes, and not suspended from any vein, then you cut it in a way like nodes, and remove it along with the part that contains the skin and bursa; otherwise, you search for its entire existence and take care of the area with something that is needed for healing until it heals.
Chapter forty-fifth.
On the cutting of types of nodes.
Of the many types of nodes, I have already said all their species in the division.
It is necessary that I explain the difference between a node and an abscess when there is doubt.
Therefore, I say that an abscess is heat and fever and violent pain until the ebullition of excess is stopped; and it is a putrid completion which now stops the fever, pain and heat.
But a node does not contain heat, nor fever nor pain; it contains that cyst lion which is at the head.
And according to the color of the body, it begins like a pimple and is made in the same way as cheese, whether large or small, and they are of two species, whether fatty and contain moisture, and the colors of moisture are many, as I said in the division.
Therefore, when you come to the treatment of a node, you expose it and investigate it at its beginning with an instrument called intromes, according to its form that will come in the chapter that is close to this one.
The method of investigation of abscesses and all nodes is that you take this instrument and insert it into the place most moist that you find in the abscess, and you turn your said instrument slowly into it until you know that the instrument has already penetrated the skin.
Then you hold your hand as close to the end as the size of the abscess allows, and then remove the instrument and examine what has come out from it.
If the flowing moisture, whatever its color, is forgotten, you cut it with a superficial incision as I have said in other abscesses.
And if there is no moisture from the instrument's probe, you know that it is fatty.
Dry it over the incision using a cross-shaped form like this: As you have learned, suspend it on one side and cut the skin all around it with ease, and keep the skin or bag if possible over it and remove the pus from it along with the node.
But if it is broken during the operation, it is not possible to remove the healthy one, and you watch carefully for it to fill up with pus, and then you remove it in pieces until there remains no cause.
For if something remains from it, either a little or too much, the node returns according to its nature.
And if you see that something small remains from it, you fill the wound with some sharp and corrosive powders and strengthen the wound, and stop it over the abscess cauterized area, and heal the other with another healing until it heals.
And if it is a large node, you sew together its two lips and heal it with what embroiders it.
But if there is pulsating vein at the opposite side, or not pulsating, you take and fill the place with a three-stranded silk that is vitriol and let it rest for two or three days until the wound heals and stops the bleeding of blood; then return to cut what has been broken from the node.

Chapter on the abscess which occurs by twisting of nerves.
Similarly, an abscess occurs in the archery and vein, and similarly it occurs in the nerves when it occurs by striking or excessive work, and so on.

The abscess is severe and is similar to the color of another body, and it is in the larger ones that are placed close together and when it is tight with pain, the patient feels as if he is in a stupor.
This abscess is not extended along the front of the body, and therefore the bandage is left open, and it is bad in every direction and does not go to the front or back.
Therefore, that which is in the joints should not be wrapped with iron, because it will cause contraction.
But that which is in the head or forehead is bandaged with sponge. If it is a small abscess, then take care of it with lancets and incise it from the root.
If it is large, then you hang it with a hook and extract it, and place it in oil; and sew the wound with suture, and treat that until it heals.

Chapter 33.
On treating scrofula (scrofula).
We have already said in the division that scrofula has a specific type and the way to treat it with medicine, and we have said that it is suspicious when cured with iron so as not to be ulcerated; and we have said that scrofula originates in the womb (uterus) and the caution of its treatment.
The ancients said that in some cases scrofula can be eradicated, such as on the skull (cranium) located at the breasts or its resemblance to other members that are used to drain it all, especially when it begins small.
But when it is old and large, you do not need to worry about it, as I cannot heal it or have not seen anyone else who has achieved this result.
The operation on it (scrofula) is when it is located as we have said, that you precede and let the patient rest and purge black bile for some days, and then fumigate it, if there is a clear filling.
Prepare the patient with preparation in which the operation is located, and prepare needles that are necessary for it; and in all ways, compress with a cloth good percrucitation (application of hot objects) until there is no cause left for its reasons. Allow the pus to run out, and do not open it lightly, but press on the places, and wash away the thick pus with your hand or an instrument that is within your reach among the instruments.
If there is opposition to a large, uncontrolled bleeding of a vein or an artery, then cauterize it where the blood flow ceases, and care for it with other treatment until it heals.

On the care of intestinal hernia.
The onset of this hernia is by a section that penetrates into the abdomen from the sides of the abdominal muscles due to which the intestines protrude through the rupture of one or more of the intestinal sacs.
This rupture can be due to the cephalic or the external part of it, and such a thing can happen in two ways for various reasons: by blows, by falls, by shouts, by an elevation caused by some grave condition, or something similar.
The sign of such (rupture), when it is due to the cephalic, is that it happens gradually over a long time, not suddenly, and it is an abscess formed around the hernia because the cephalic compresses the intestine.
The sign of such (rupture), when it is due to the section of the cephalic, is that at the beginning it causes a strong sudden pain; and the abscess appears in various places other than the natural opening, which is indeed the intestine itself, and the body swells in the parts outside the cephalic.
And in some cases the intestine is forgotten and this hernia is called strangulated intestinal hernia, zirbal.
And in some cases it is done with the windbag (enema), and in some cases the intestine tears, and it remains, and this is a very serious danger to the patient, and in some cases it causes bad and worsening pain especially when it is pressed.
And in the treatment of this disease, fear arises, so that care should be taken to avoid hunting in such a case.
The method of the operation for such is to command the patient to return the intestine with his own hands inside its cavity, if he can, and to place a bandage over it on its backside, and raise the legs upwards.
Place a bandage that cuts the opening of the scrotum in half, and cut through the scrotum completely from top to bottom; and insert two fingers into the incision as needed to divide the incision with them.
If the incision is made according to the amount that you can possibly forget about that (the intestine).
Place the hernia sac outside the scrotum until the white hard cephalic is found in each part.
You insert your finger into the hernia sac that is between the white cephalic and the testicle, and separate the cephalic according to its position, and free it from any adhesion that is in the back of the hernia sac.
Place your hand on the scrotum in each part, and with that extend the white cephalic in each place with your left hand, and lift the testicle with the cephalic to the incision site; and command the assistant to stretch the hernia sac and you dissolve the adhesion that is behind it with complete solution.
Search for any cause of the intestine being enveloped in the white hard cephalic. If you find such a cause, then remove it from the abdomen.
Place an incision in the back of the scrotum according to the section that flows blood and pus as we have recommended in what has been said.
Place a linen bandage soaked in oil and wait on the wound; and administer the binding that we have recommended (and sometimes the white cephalic is cauterized, which has been mentioned to prevent blood flow, as this often happens), and leave the binding until it falls off by itself.
If hunting is delayed, soak the wound in hot water and wait on it until it falls off as we have said.
Care for the wound with the other care of wounds until it is healed.
Chapter 66.
On hernia ventosa (windbag).
In this hernia, no one has been seen to be cured by surgery.
At first they said that the hernia due to water should be treated thus as we have recommended in hernia with urine; which is to tie the vessels near the incision with ease; and to cut in the middle where the abscess is formed around it, until the vessels fall off.
Tend to the wound according to what has been said until it heals.

Chapter LXVIII.
On the softening of the scrotum of the testicles.
In certain men, the scrotum of the testicles becomes softened because the flesh between it is softened, and its treatment should be given attention to.
Therefore, it is necessary for the one treating the condition to make the patient lie on his side, and completely separate the scrotum that has become softened from the natural scrotum; and then sew together two lips with stitches.
And if you wish, cut off the excess of the softened scrotum with three or four stitches and secure a firm stitch.
Then close the incision between the stitches, and care for other afflictions until they are healed and the pain subsides.
Chapter 69.
On castration.
Know that castration is prohibited by our law, but for the sake of my memory I recall it in this book; and it is not necessary to remember it except in two ways: one because the doctor who is asked about it knows its treatment if it occurs; and the other way is that we often have need for castration of other animals for the benefit of our use, such as with horses, cattle, pigs, and similar animals.
And so I say that castration is performed in two ways: either by strangulation, or by incision and sectioning.
But in the method of strangulation, the procedure is to seize the animal by its tail before its testicles are softened and lined up. Then hold them with your hand until they become resolved and do not appear again.
But in castration by incision and sectioning, it is necessary that you have the animal and press the scrotum of the testicles with your left hand.
Then lift the spermatic cord and make an incision over each vessel to a depth of two fingers.
And make an incision in any pus that you may have to drain it. Do not leave any cause for the abscess, but only the fine one that is on the veins.
This method of castration is better when performed by strangulation because strangulation quickly eliminates any cause for the testicles to desire coit.
Care for the wound until it heals.
Chapter 70.
On the treatment of hermaphrodism.
Hermaphrodism in men occurs in two ways: one is when a gap appears in the scrotum between the testicles, and within it there is a conch-like formation that resembles female genitals with hairs.
And certain cases of a hernia in which urine collects in the scrotum.
In women, there is a special case: and it is that the conch of a woman on the pelvis is similar to two testicles of a man with only a small part protruding from the vaginal opening like male genitals and two testicles.
The treatment is in three types: for one type of men and for one type of women. It is necessary to make an incision and drain the inflammation of that area until the condition improves, and then care for it with other treatments.
In the second type of male ailment where urine is in the scrotum of the testicles, there is neither cure nor operation on it.
Capitulo xxi. (in English: Chapter XXI)
Of prolonged and prominent flesh due to female causes.
Prolonged swelling due to natural causes is reduced and properly treated with the right regimen, but sometimes it becomes exacerbated in certain women so much that it spreads like in men and reaches the vagina.
Therefore, you should remove the excess swelling with your hand or oil and incise it.
And do not continue incising, especially at the root of the lesion, to avoid bleeding.
And take care of that wound until it heals.
Flesh born is flesh that grows within the womb of a woman until it fills it up, and prolonged swelling is like this (and for this reason some people call it “caudated disease”); therefore we incise it as we would an abscess, and treat it until it heals.
Capitolo LXXII. (in English: Chapter LXXII)
Of the treatment of arthritis.
Arthritis is a condition where the cervix does not open or it is narrow. It can be either natural or accidental.
Accidental is due to disease that has occurred before, and it is caused either by swelling of the flesh not properly reduced or by cysts that are subtle or large.
It is caused either in the root of the uterus or in its costae (or sides), or on the superficial pus or deep pus, and it forbids coitus, engagement, and conception, and strongly prohibits menstruation.
The recognition of this condition is made by the midwife if the opening is visible, but if it is not, you must seek for it with fingers or with a rod.
If the opening is due to a subtle cyst that is close to the two labiae, you must break it and separate it.
This means that you place your fingers between the two labiae, and indicate with both hands in which direction to proceed.
The woman lies on her back with her legs extended and you spread the two labiae apart with force until that subtle cyst is broken and the opening is opened up.
Take wool, dip it in oil and place it over the area, and leave it for a day to ensure that the incision site does not become consolidated.
But if the cyst is large and thick, you must incise it with a spatula or a leaf of myrtle.
But if the opening is due to fibrosis, you must suspend it with oil and incise it.
And use the medications that stop bleeding without causing pain, such as henbane, dragon's blood, and poppy seeds, mixed with albumen of egg whites.
And administer a wide lead cannula to ensure that the wound does not heal easily.
Keep it for several days and administer hot water poultices.
And let it be cured by other methods of consolidation until it is healed.
Sometimes the uterus expels other fleshy substances during childbirth, and it is necessary to incise them according to this method. But if it is an abscess containing cancerous matter in the uterus, do not apply iron to it in any way.

Chapter LXXVI (76 in Roman numerals).
On extracting a dead fetus.
When treating a dead fetus as mentioned in the division of medicine and it has not been expelled yet, you must determine if the woman is of good moral character and not subject to any accidents that are feared for her safety.
The woman should be positioned lying on her left side, and her head should be tilted downward, with her hips raised.

If there is bleeding, then stop it with styptic waters and administer the other treatment.

Treatment for fistulas that run downwards.
Fistulas that run downward in the lower part are nodular and swollen, which run towards the anus outside or in the space of one partition.

Sometimes those fistulas can be observed penetrating into the bladder space and into the meat of the penis, and sometimes they penetrate into the joint of the hip and into the navel.
Fistula penetrating into the anus but not outside is known as when you insert your finger in the anus and try to find the fistula with a subtle probe or iron, if it is not treacherous.

But if it penetrates into the joint of the hip or bone and pain is encountered in the area, this signifies that if the probe can enter the bone without treachery, pain will be felt in the surrounding area; that pus forms quickly; and that no medication works there, nor does it heal with salve.
And in all those penetrating fistulas, there is no cure for them all, and the cure of these is the labor and futility of foolish doctors over which they are obsessed.
